## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics / growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an ODE right-hand-side for population size P evolving in time t, which is classic single-species population dynamics. Common structures capture density-independent growth, density dependence (carrying capacity), Allee effects at low density, and time-varying forcing such as seasonality or harvesting.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Linear growth with immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net constant influx/outflux plus proportional growth)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (self-limitation or facilitation approximated by a low-order polynomial)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order crowding/complex density effects)
- Verhulst (logistic ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying capacity encoded by a linear crowding term)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (decelerating growth with multiplicative log-distance to capacity)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized density dependence; curvature controlled by exponent)
- Richards-type growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (flexible sigmoid approach to capacity)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (growth negative below a critical abundance)
- Allee effect (weak, saturating facilitation): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (P / (P + c2)) (low-density suppression that vanishes at high P)
- Constant harvesting (removal): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed quota removal)
- Proportional harvesting (mortality): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (per-capita removal or death)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Seasonally forced carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4))) (resource availability oscillates with time)
- Time-varying trend in growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P - c2 * P**2 (gradual change in conditions producing nonstationary parameters)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-independent growth typically appears as a term proportional to P (per-capita rate approximately constant).
- Carrying-capacity limitation is often encoded by a multiplicative crowding factor like (1 - c*P) or (1 - (c*P)**theta), producing a zero-growth equilibrium at high P.
- Gompertz-type regulation introduces log(c/P) or -log(P) with a prefactor P, reflecting regulation proportional to log-distance from capacity.
- Allee effects create an additional low-density factor (c*P - 1) or P/(P + c), yielding negative growth below a threshold or suppressed growth near P≈0.
- Harvesting or external mortality is indicated by subtractive terms: constant removal (-c) versus proportional removal (-c*P).
- Seasonality or cyclical environment commonly yields sin(c*t + phase) or cos(c*t + phase) modulating per-capita growth or capacity.
- Nonstationary environments can be captured by parameters drifting with t (e.g., c0 + c1*t), which changes growth rate over time even at fixed P.
- Multiple equilibria (bistability) often corresponds to polynomial-in-P right-hand sides with multiple real roots (e.g., P*(a + b*P + c*P**2)).

Fitted params       : c0=-1.0947e-02, c1=5.2098e-01, c2=-1.2534e-13, c3=-3.2496e+00, c4=2.0000e+00, c5=-1.6216e-02, c6=1.3275e-01, c7=5.2098e-01

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG5)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P**c4/(c5*P + c6)
Candidate formulas: 73

Let \(P\) be the only feature actually used by the GT (the GT is independent of \(t\)). Rewrite the GT into a simple canonical form.

### Ground Truth (fixed function)
\[
0.9198344660\,(1-\tfrac{P}{84.0283518631})P \;+\; 0.9198344660\,\frac{P^2}{7.5314755755\,P+1}
\]
Expand the first part:
\[
0.9198344660\,P \;-\;\Big(\frac{0.9198344660}{84.0283518631}\Big)P^2 \;+\; 0.9198344660\,\frac{P^2}{7.5314755755\,P+1}
\]
So GT has exactly:
- a linear term \(aP\),
- a quadratic polynomial term \(bP^2\) (with \(b<0\)),
- plus a **rational** term of the form \(\dfrac{kP^2}{\alpha P+1}\),
and **no** constants, no \(1/P\) terms, no logs/exp/trig, no \(t\)-dependence.

A candidate can only match if it can be set to exactly this structure for all \(P\).

---

## Candidate-by-candidate analysis

### 1. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2(Pc3)^{c4} + \frac{Pc5}{P+c6} + Pc7\)
Has rational term \(\frac{Pc5}{P+c6}\) (numerator degree 1), but GT needs \(\frac{P^2}{\alpha P+1}\) (numerator degree 2). The extra \(Pc2(Pc3)^{c4}\) is a power term; to avoid mismatch must be killed (set \(c2=0\)). Then still only \(\frac{P}{P+c6}\), cannot become \(\frac{P^2}{\alpha P+1}\) for all \(P\). **No.**

### 2. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2(1-(Pc3)^{c4})^{c5} + c6 + c7/P\)
Contains constant \(c6\) and \(c7/P\); GT has neither, so must set \(c6=c7=0\). Remaining nonlinear \((1-(Pc3)^{c4})^{c5}\) cannot equal \(\frac{P^2}{\alpha P+1}\) for all \(P\) (wrong functional family). **No.**

### 3. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2(1-(Pc3)^{c4})^{c5}\)
Same issue: last term is not a rational \(\frac{P^2}{\alpha P+1}\) unless it is forced to 0 (then GT’s rational part missing). **No.**

### 4. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + P^2c3 + Pc4 + Pc5 + \frac{Pc6}{P+c7}\)
Has \(P^3\) unless \(c0=0\). Then polynomial part is at most \(P^2\) plus \(\frac{P}{P+c7}\). Again numerator degree 1 in rational term, cannot match GT’s \(\frac{P^2}{\alpha P+1}\). **No.**

### 5. \(\frac{P^3c0}{P+c1} + \frac{P^2c2}{P+c1} + Pc3 + Pc4(Pc5)^{c6}\)
The first two share denominator \(P+c1\): combine to \(\frac{P^2(c0P+c2)}{P+c1}\), which generally has a \(P^3/(P+c1)\) component. To avoid extra structure, set \(c0=0\), leaving \(\frac{P^2c2}{P+c1}\) which matches GT’s rational *shape* if we set \(c1=1/7.5314...\)?? Careful: GT denominator is \((7.5314)P+1\), i.e. proportional to \(P+\frac{1}{7.5314}\). Indeed
\[
\frac{P^2}{7.5314P+1}=\frac{1}{7.5314}\cdot \frac{P^2}{P+\frac{1}{7.5314}}
\]
So \(\frac{P^2c2}{P+c1}\) can match the rational term by choosing \(c1=\frac{1}{7.5314...}\) and \(c2=\frac{0.9198344660}{7.5314...}\).
But candidate 5 also has \(Pc4(Pc5)^{c6}\). To match GT, this must reduce to a polynomial term already present (linear or quadratic). If \(c6=0\), it becomes \(Pc4\) (linear), which can be absorbed into \(Pc3\). If \(c6=1\), it becomes \(P^2(c4c5)\) (quadratic), which could match the GT quadratic coefficient. Great: we can set \(c6=1\) and tune \(c4c5\) to the needed quadratic coefficient, and tune \(c3\) to the needed linear coefficient.
Thus candidate 5 **can** represent:
- linear term via \(Pc3\),
- quadratic term via \(Pc4(Pc5)^{1}=c4c5\,P^2\),
- rational term via \(\frac{P^2c2}{P+c1}\) with \(c0=0\).
So **Yes, candidate 5 can match GT.**

### 6. \(\frac{P\cdot P^{c0}c1}{P+c2} + \frac{Pc3}{P+c2} + \frac{P^{c0}c4}{P+c2}\)
All terms share denominator \(P+c2\), giving \(\frac{c1P^{c0+1}+c3P+c4P^{c0}}{P+c2}\). GT has also a *polynomial part outside* the rational term; here everything is rational unless numerator cancels denominator to yield polynomial, but then you lose the needed “polynomial + rational” decomposition with different denominators. Also matching \(\frac{P^2}{\alpha P+1}\) while also producing separate polynomial terms is not feasible. **No.**

### 7. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + \frac{Pc3}{P+c4} + Pc5\)
Rational term has numerator degree 1, not 2. **No.**

### 8. \(\frac{Pc0}{P+c1} + Pc2(Pc3)^{c4} + Pc5\)
Rational term is \(\frac{P}{P+c1}\) not \(\frac{P^2}{\alpha P+1}\). **No.**

### 9. \(\frac{P^3c0}{P+c1} + P^3c2 + P^2c3 + P^2c4 + \frac{P^2c5}{P+c1} + Pc6\)
Has \(P^3c2\) unless \(c2=0\). Also \(\frac{P^3c0}{P+c1}\) introduces a \(P^2\) polynomial part plus extra rational behavior unless \(c0=0\). If \(c0=0\), rational becomes \(\frac{P^2c5}{P+c1}\) (good), and polynomial terms can match. So structurally it could match like candidate 5. However it has *two* independent \(P^2\) coefficients (c3,c4) which is fine. Therefore this also seems potentially matchable by setting \(c0=0,c2=0\). Denominator can be matched as before. So **Yes, candidate 9 can match GT** (it contains candidate-5-like substructure).

### 10. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + \frac{Pc3}{P+c4} + Pc5\)
Rational numerator degree 1. **No.**

### 11. \(\frac{P^3c0}{P+c1} + \frac{P^2c2}{P+c1} + Pc3\)
Combine first two: \(\frac{P^2(c0P+c2)}{P+c1}\). To avoid extra \(P^3/(P+c1)\) component, set \(c0=0\), leaving \(\frac{P^2c2}{P+c1}+Pc3\). This matches GT’s rational term and linear term, but GT also has an *independent quadratic polynomial* term \(-\beta P^2\) outside the rational. Candidate 11 has no standalone \(P^2\) term. Could \(\frac{P^2c2}{P+c1}\) be decomposed into polynomial + rational to supply that? Long division:
\[
\frac{P^2}{P+c1}=P-c1+\frac{c1^2}{P+c1}
\]
This produces a linear and constant term, not a \(P^2\) term. So cannot generate the needed standalone quadratic coefficient. **No.**

### 12–14,18,21–23 (many terms all over \(P+c1\))
All these are sums of terms each with denominator \(P+c1\), i.e. overall \(\frac{\text{poly}(P)}{P+c1}\). Such forms, after division, yield at most a polynomial plus a remainder \(\frac{\text{const}}{P+c1}\). GT’s rational part is \(\frac{P^2}{P+c}\) (after scaling), whose remainder is constant over \(P+c\), but GT also needs a standalone \(P^2\) polynomial term. A \(\frac{\text{poly}}{P+c1}\) can indeed yield a \(P^2\) polynomial term if numerator degree is 3: \(\frac{P^3}{P+c1}=P^2-c1P+c1^2-\frac{c1^3}{P+c1}\). That gives a \(P^2\) polynomial term, but then the remainder is \(\frac{\text{const}}{P+c1}\), not \(\frac{P^2}{P+c1}\). GT specifically needs remainder proportional to \(\frac{P^2}{P+c1}\), not \(\frac{1}{P+c1}\). So these cannot match exactly unless you reintroduce \(\frac{P^2}{P+c1}\) explicitly, which these forms don’t (they only have \(P^k/(P+c1)\) with \(k\le 3\), but combining them still yields remainder constant, not \(P^2\)). Therefore **No** for 12,13,14,18,21,22,23.

### 15. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + \frac{Pc2}{P+c3}\)
Rational numerator degree 1. **No.**

### 16. Adds \((1-(Pc5)^{c6})^{c7}\) term; cannot create needed rational. **No.**

### 17. \(\frac{P^3c0}{P+c1} + P^2c2 + \frac{P^2c3}{P+c1} + Pc4 + \frac{Pc5}{P+c6}\)
Has an extra \(\frac{P}{P+c6}\) term; must set \(c5=0\). Then we have \(\frac{P^3c0+P^2c3}{P+c1}+P^2c2+Pc4\). As with candidate 11, if \(c0\neq 0\) you get remainder constant over \(P+c1\); if \(c0=0\) you get \(\frac{P^2c3}{P+c1}\) (good) plus standalone \(P^2c2\) (good) plus linear \(Pc4\) (good). Denominator can be matched. So **Yes, candidate 17 can match GT** by setting \(c0=0,c5=0\) and tuning \(c1,c2,c3,c4\).

### 19. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 + \frac{Pc3}{P+c4}\)
Has constant \(Pc2\) actually linear? Wait \(P*c2\) yes linear; still rational numerator degree 1. **No.**

### 20. \(\frac{P^3c0}{P+c1} + P^2c2 + \frac{P^2c3}{P+c1} + Pc4\)
Same reasoning as 17 without the extra \(\frac{P}{P+c6}\). Set \(c0=0\) to avoid wrong remainder type, leaving \(\frac{P^2c3}{P+c1}+P^2c2+Pc4\). This matches GT structure. **Yes, candidate 20 can match GT.**

### 24–43,45–46,48–59,61–66,68–69,71–73
All of these introduce logs/exp/trig/Abs/t dependence or \(1/P\) terms. Since GT has none of these, the only way is to set their coefficients to 0. After zeroing, what remains in each case is one of the already-checked base rational forms:
- Many reduce to candidate 15/10/19 type with \(\frac{P}{P+c}\) (cannot).
- Some reduce to candidate 11 type lacking standalone \(P^2\) (cannot).
- Some reduce to candidate 20/17 type (can), but only if they actually contain \(\frac{P^2}{P+c}\) plus standalone \(P^2\) and \(P\).

Checking quickly:
- 25 reduces to candidate 20 plus log term; set log coeff 0 → becomes candidate 20 form → **matchable**.
- 57 reduces to candidate 20 plus \(P\log(1+c/P)\); set that coeff 0 → candidate 20 form → **matchable**.
- 61 has cosine term; set its coeff 0 → becomes candidate 11 form (no standalone \(P^2\)) unless \(c0=0\) etc; but still lacks standalone \(P^2\) → **not**.
- 44/47/52/60 etc depend on \(t\) inside cos/exp; can be zeroed, leaving candidate 11 form (no standalone \(P^2\)) → **not**.
- 59/62 etc are \(P^2+P+\frac{P}{P+c}\) types → **not**.

So additional **matchable** ones: **25 and 57**.

### 26–27,29–35,37–43,46,51,53–56,58,63–70,72–73
After attempting to zero non-algebraic parts, none leave exactly the needed combination \((\text{linear})+(\text{quadratic})+\frac{P^2}{P+c}\) except those already identified (25,57). The rest either:
- have only \(\frac{P}{P+c}\),
- or have all terms over one denominator,
- or introduce unavoidable non-polynomial/non-rational dependence.

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare each candidate to it.

**GT expression:**
$$f(P) = 0.9198 \cdot (1 - P/84.03) \cdot P + 0.9198 \cdot P^2 / (7.531P + 1)$$

Let me expand this:
$$f(P) = 0.9198P - 0.9198P^2/84.03 + 0.9198P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$
$$= 0.9198P - 0.01095P^2 + 0.9198P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$

So the GT has the form: **aP + bP² + cP²/(dP + e)** where a, b, c, d, e are specific constants.

Note that GT depends only on P, not on t. Any candidate with t-dependence that cannot be zeroed out is a NO MATCH.

Let me also write GT with a common denominator over (dP+1):
$$f(P) = \frac{(0.9198P - 0.01095P^2)(7.531P+1) + 0.9198P^2}{7.531P+1}$$

Numerator: $0.9198P \cdot 7.531P + 0.9198P - 0.01095P^2 \cdot 7.531P - 0.01095P^2 + 0.9198P^2$
$= 6.927P^2 + 0.9198P - 0.08246P^3 - 0.01095P^2 + 0.9198P^2$
$= -0.08246P^3 + (6.927 - 0.01095 + 0.9198)P^2 + 0.9198P$
$= -0.08246P^3 + 7.836P^2 + 0.9198P$

So: $f(P) = \frac{-0.08246P^3 + 7.836P^2 + 0.9198P}{7.531P + 1}$

This can be factored as: $f(P) = \frac{P(-0.08246P^2 + 7.836P + 0.9198)}{7.531P + 1}$

The GT structural form is: **αP² + βP + γP²/(δP + ε)** — a polynomial in P plus a rational function of P.

**Candidate 1:** `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2(Pc3)^c4 + Pc5/(P+c6) + Pc7`

Wait, but we also have the P²c0 term. The GT is aP² + bP + cP²/(dP+e). Candidate 1 has P²·A + P·B + P·c5/(P+c6). The rational part is P/(P+c6) vs P²/(dP+e). These are linearly independent rational functions, so we can't match.

Actually wait - let me reconsider. We need to check if the full expression can match. Let me put GT over common denominator: (-0.08246P³ + 7.836P² + 0.9198P)/(7.531P+1).

Numerator of GT: -0.08246P³ + 7.836P² + 0.9198P

- c2+c3 = 7.836/7.531 = 1.0405
- c3c1 = 0.9198/7.531 → c3 = 0.9198 → c3·(1/7.531) = 0.1221... but 0.9198/7.531 = 0.1221. And c3 = 0.9198/7.531... wait.

Actually, c3c1 = 0.9198/7.531 = 0.1221. With c1 = 1/7.531 = 0.1328, c3 = 0.1221/0.1328 = 0.9194. Then c2 = 1.0405 - 0.9194 = 0.1211.

All solvable. Works!

Candidate 11 verdict: [MATCH]

---

**Candidate 12:** `P³c0/(P+c1) + P³c2/(P+c1) + P²c3/(P+c1) + P²c4/(P+c1) + P²c5/(P+c1) + P²c6/(P+c1) + Pc7/(P+c1) + Pc8/(P+c1) + Pc9/(P+c1)`

= [(c0+c2)P³ + (c3+c4+c5+c6)P² + (c7+c8+c9)P]/(P+c1)

This is cubic/linear. Same form as GT. Works.

**Candidate 15:** `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2/(P+c3)`

Over common denominator: [c0P²(P+c3) + c1P(P+c3) + c2P]/(P+c3)
= [c0P³ + c0c3P² + c1P² + c1c3P + c2P]/(P+c3)
= [c0P³ + (c0c3+c1)P² + (c1c3+c2)P]/(P+c3)

Cubic/linear. But we have 3 free constants (c0,c1,c2,c3 = 4) and need to match 4 parameters (cubic coeff, quadratic coeff, linear coeff, denominator constant). 

GT: (-0.08246P³ + 7.836P² + 0.9198P)/(7.531P+1)

c3 = 1/7.531. Then:
- c0 = -0.08246/7.531 = -0.01095
- c0c3 + c1 = 7.836/7.531 → -0.01095/7.531 + c1 = 1.0405 → c1 = 1.042
- c1c3 + c2 = 0.9198/7.531 → 1.042/7.531 + c2 = 0.1221 → c2 = -0.0163

All solvable! Works.

Candidate 15 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 17:** `P³c0/(P+c1) + P²c2 + P²c3/(P+c1) + Pc4 + Pc5/(P+c6)`

This has TWO different denominators: (P+c1) and (P+c6). Over common denominator (P+c1)(P+c6):

[c0P³(P+c6) + c2P²(P+c1)(P+c6) + c3P²(P+c6) + c4P(P+c1)(P+c6) + c5P(P+c1)] / [(P+c1)(P+c6)]

The c2P² term gives P⁴. Setting c2=0:
[c0P³(P+c6) + c3P²(P+c6) + c4P(P+c1)(P+c6) + c5P(P+c1)] / [(P+c1)(P+c6)]

Still has P⁴ from c0P³·(P+c6) and c4P·(P+c1)(P+c6). This is more complex than GT.

But wait - can we set c1=c6? Then denominator is (P+c1)². GT has denominator (7.531P+1) which is linear. A squared denominator can't match a linear denominator unless... no, they're fundamentally different.

Alternatively, can we set c0=0 and c4=0? Then: [c3P²(P+c6) + c5P(P+c1)] / [(P+c1)(P+c6)]. This doesn't simplify to cubic/linear unless c1=c6.

If c1=c6: [c3P²(P+c1) + c5P(P+c1)] / (P+c1)² = [c3P² + c5P]/(P+c1). This is quadratic/linear, but GT is cubic/linear. Not enough degrees of freedom.

Let me try differently. Set c5=0: [c0P³(P+c6) + c2P²(P+c1)(P+c6) + c3P²(P+c6) + c4P(P+c1)(P+c6)] / [(P+c1)(P+c6)]

Set c2=0: [c0P³(P+c6) + c3P²(P+c6) + c4P(P+c1)(P+c6)] / [(P+c1)(P+c6)]
= [c0P³ + c3P² + c4P(P+c1)] / (P+c1)  [canceling (P+c6)]
= [c0P³ + c3P² + c4P² + c4c1P] / (P+c1)
= [c0P³ + (c3+c4)P² + c4c1P] / (P+c1)

This is cubic/linear! Works.

**Candidate 67:** `P³c0/(P+c1) + P²c2/(P+c1) + Pc3·(c4-(Pc5)^c6)^c7`

Setting c6=1, c7=-1: Pc3·(c4-Pc5)^(-1) = Pc3/(c4-Pc5) = -c3P/(c5P-c4) = c3P/(c4-c5P). This is P/(linear in P).

Total: [c0P³+c2P²]/(P+c1) + c3P/(c4-c5P).

Over common denominator (P+c1)(c4-c5P):
[c0P³(c4-c5P) + c2P²(c4-c5P) + c3P(P+c1)] / [(P+c1)(c4-c5P)]

This has P⁴ term (-c0c5P⁴). Setting c0=0:
[c2P²(c4-c5P) + c3P(P+c1)] / [(P+c1)(c4-c5P)]
= [c2c4P² - c2c5P³ + c3P² + c3c1P] / [(P+c1)(c4-c5P)]
= [-c2c5P³ + (c2c4+c3)P² + c3c1P] / [(P+c1)(c4-c5P)]

GT denominator is linear (7.531P+1). This denominator is quadratic. For it to reduce, we'd need cancellation. The numerator is cubic. For the quadratic denominator to simplify to linear, we'd need one factor to cancel. This is possible if the numerator is divisible by one of the factors.
